Email, inside look

I work as a system administrator in one company. And then there was an interesting situation with sending some information to us by e-mail. In order not to go into details with the actual situation (it comes to tender proposals, where there is a huge amount of conditions), I will give my example.

We received two files in the mail.



However, the sender by all means claims that all three files have been sent to us, and the following screenshot is sent to prove his words:



Here, even an ordinary person can understand that this can be a modified pattern.

If we are wrong, we can get a penalty, if we are right, we must prove it. And here we start to understand. Once I read that a letter should have a property, and after a successful first google request we find a hint: file -> Property, and we get what we need.



For convenience, we copy all of this into a text file and start learning (email and ip addresses and domains have been replaced).

Writing property

Based on intuition and all the same google we start to study:

As the Internet says - you need to read the file from the bottom up. Immediately go the informational headers "X -...", which are added for additional information (in our case from the mailer and the antivirus). We omit them. The next line Received-SPF is a check of the correspondence of the sender's domain to its IP address, since phishers may confuse domain substitution users. 

 Received-SPF: Pass (edge.contoso.com: domain of –û—Ç–ø—Ä–∞–≤–∏—Ç–µ–ª—å@yandex.ru designates 37.140.190.176 as permitted sender) receiver=edge.contoso.com; client-ip=37.140.190.176; helo=forward400o.mail.yandex.net;

Nslookup, and we see that the ip address and belongs to mail.yandex. 

 Name: forward400o.mail.yandex.net Address: 37.140.190.176

The following is the sender of the letter: 

 Return-Path: –û—Ç–ø—Ä–∞–≤–∏—Ç–µ–ª—å@yandex.ru

The next line is some separator, we will remember this. 

 ------==--bound.201681.myt4-c0b480c282c8.qloud-c.yandex.net--

Also, for the time being, omit the line: 

 Content-Type: multipart/mixed;

We stop at the Message-Id - this is a unique identifier (UID) of the digital message, which is guaranteed not to be repeated. We will also return to it later. 

 Message-Id: <57782461549623787@myt5-96980ae04900.qloud-c.yandex.net>
Next line with the date and time. 

 Date: Fri, 8 Feb 2019 14:02:31 +0300

Then comes the subject of the letter: 

 Subject: =?utf- 8?B?0JLQvtGCINCy0LDRiNC4INC+0LHQtdGJ0LDQvdC90YvQtSDQutCw0YDRgtC40L3QutC4IQ==?=

It is encoded in Base 64 and to read it, we come to the aid of the site: www.online-decoder.com/ru .

Specify the encoding type base64 and UTF-8. You can also click "Selection", and the system will try to pick it up.



It turned out our theme: " Here are your promised pictures ." It is worth noting that the text of the topic itself is enclosed in question marks The subject line looks like: 

 0JLQvtGCINCy0LDRiNC4INC+0LHQtdGJ0LDQvdC90YvQtSDQutCw0YDRgtC40L3QutC4IQ=

Next: " To: <Recipient@contoso.com> " - the recipient, followed by two lines of the sender: " Envelope-From: Sender@yandex.by " and " From: =? Utf-8? B? 0JLQsNGB0LjQu9C40Lkg0J / Rg9C / 0LrQuNC9 ? = ". As far as I understand, the Envelope-From: field contains the real sender of the letter, and in the From: field, whatever you want, this field is displayed in the received letter and often changes during phishing.

In the " From: " line, something is encoded again: 

 Envelope-From: –û—Ç–ø—Ä–∞–≤–∏—Ç–µ–ª—å@yandex.by From: =?utf-8?B?0JLQsNGB0LjQu9C40Lkg0J/Rg9C/0LrQuNC9?= <–û—Ç–ø—Ä–∞–≤–∏—Ç–µ–ª—å@yandex.ru>

Using the same service, we see that the name of the sender is "Vasily Pupkin"
Next DKIM-Signature - E-mail authentication method. And Authentication-Results - contains the results of various authentication checks for SMTP messages, such as SPF, DKIM, and SMTP authentication.

Received - means that the letter after sending was received on one of the servers (in this case, the Yandex server) at 2:02:31 PM (+0300 means time zone): 

 Received: by myt4-c0b480c282c8.qloud-c.yandex.net with HTTP; Fri, 08 Feb 2019 14:02:31 +0300

All further Received lines indicate that the letter ‚Äúwalked‚Äù from server to server until it reached the recipient, and each server made a note about it.

A detailed study shows that a letter from yandex.net got on our internal server, edge.contoso.com . 

 Received: from forward400o.mail.yandex.net (37.140.190.176) by edge.contoso.com (192.168.10.1) with Microsoft SMTP Server id 14.3.399.0; Fri, 8 Feb 2019 14:02:18 +0300

By the way, this line specifically helped us out once, when a dispute came in, but the code came all the same to us on the server. The mail servers of some organizations due to some of their delays send mail for a long time. But we have everything with this strictly.

So far, I do not understand one thing, the letter went from the sender at 14:02:31 , and it came to us at 14:02:18 . I suppose that some difference in time between our server and Yandex server.

Recieved 
 Received: from forward400o.mail.yandex.net (37.140.190.176) by edge.contoso.com (192.168.50.20) with Microsoft SMTP Server id 14.3.399.0; Fri, 8 Feb 2019 14:02:18 +0300 Received: from mxback17g.mail.yandex.net (mxback17g.mail.yandex.net [IPv6:2a02:6b8:0:1472:2741:0:8b7:317]) by forward400o.mail.yandex.net (Yandex) with ESMTP id 4C06A14C0F30 for <–ü–æ–ª—É—á–∞—Ç–µ–ª—å@contoso.com>; Fri, 8 Feb 2019 14:02:32 +0300 (MSK) Received: from localhost (localhost [::1]) by mxback17g.mail.yandex.net (nwsmtp/Yandex) with ESMTP id RqfUyfuyVt-2VoiJWwn; Fri, 08 Feb 2019 14:02:31 +0300


To analyze the letter headers, especially lazy, you can also use the service .

Below is a screenshot of the analyzer results:



So, there is nothing interesting here, well, then it means that you need to receive the headers of the sent letter and verify it.

We contact the office and ask them to send the same headlines. Since on that side there will most likely be an ordinary user, we drop the instruction.

In the sent letter you need to click on the three horizontal points -> Letter property. All contents are saved to a text file and reset to us in the box.



We were sent a file in which more than 2000 lines!
